\section{Block 5--6 Results (Iters 307--313)}
\label{sec:block56}

\subsection{Factor-of-6 Upgraded from Axiom to Theorem (Iter 307)}
\label{sec:factor6-theorem}

The coefficient $6$ in $\mu = 6\pi^5[\cdots]$ was previously classified as a
Category~C structural axiom identified with $\binom{4}{2}$ bivectors but without
a derivation.  Iter~307 closed this gap: four independent representation-theoretic
proofs now establish $6 = C(4,2)$ as a \emph{theorem}:

\begin{theorem}[Factor-of-6, Iter 307]
The coefficient $6$ in $\mu = 6\pi^5$ equals $C(4,2) = 6$ by four independent
representation-theoretic routes:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item \textbf{Bivector counting.} $\Lambda^2(\mathbb{R}^4) = 6$; the six
        independent 2-forms of $\mathbb{R}^4$ label the topological flux channels
        of the Clifford pseudoscalar.
  \item \textbf{SO(4) chirality.} Parity in SO(4) forces both chiral SU(2)
        factors to contribute; each carries 3 generators, giving $3 + 3 = 6$
        (no cancellation possible).
  \item \textbf{E8 branching.} The decomposition
        $\mathrm{E}_8 \supset \mathrm{SO}(10)\times\mathrm{SU}(4)$ yields a
        $(10,6)$ representation; the factor~6 is the dimension of the
        $\mathbf{6}$ of SU(4).
  \item \textbf{Hodge self-duality.} $\Lambda^2(\mathbb{R}^4)$ is the unique
        self-dual exterior power in four dimensions (Hodge star maps
        $\Omega^2 \to \Omega^2$); self-duality fixes the multiplicity to 6.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\noindent
This result upgrades the discrete-choice classification of coefficient~6
from Category~C (axiom) to Category~B (derived), reducing the complexity
ledger by $\sim 1$~bit.  It also removes the only remaining axiom in the mass
formula: $\mu = 6\pi^5$ is now fully derived from Clifford/SO(4) geometry and
the 7-design structure of E8 (see Sec.~\ref{sec:7design}).

\subsection{3837 = $128\times 30 - 3$: Representation-Theoretic Decomposition (Iter 308)}
\label{sec:3837-repthy}

The previous identification $3837 = 8\times 480 - 3$ (Law~II + G$_2$ correction)
is supplemented by a spinor-algebraic decomposition discovered in iter~308:
\begin{equation}
  3837 = \dim(S^+_{16})\times h(\mathrm{E}_8) - |\Phi^+_{\mathrm{short}}(\mathrm{G}_2)|
       = 128 \times 30 - 3
\end{equation}
where $S^+_{16} = 128$ is the positive-chirality half-spinor representation of
SO(16), $h(\mathrm{E}_8) = 30$ is the E8 Coxeter number, and
$|\Phi^+_{\mathrm{short}}(\mathrm{G}_2)| = 3$ counts the positive short roots
of G$_2$.  The bridging identity
\begin{equation}
  128\times 30 - 137\times 28 = 4 = \mathrm{rank}(\mathrm{F}_4)
\end{equation}
connects the half-spinor dimension, the E8 Coxeter number, and the integer part
of $1/\alpha$ to the rank of F$_4$.  The decomposition is a mathematical identity;
it provides a spinor-clock narrative for 3837 but does not yet constitute a
dynamical derivation of $\alpha$.

\subsection{The $-3$ Correction: G$_2$ Triality Redundancy (Iter 322)}
\label{sec:3837-triality}

The correction $3840 - 3 = 3837$ acquires a precise geometric meaning via the
outer-automorphism group of D$_4$.  The triality group
$\mathrm{Out}(\mathrm{D}_4) \cong S_3$ acts on the three eight-dimensional
representations of SO(8)---the vector, and the two half-spinors---permuting
them by a symmetry of the Dynkin diagram.  Under this action, G$_2$ embeds in
SO(8) with \emph{three} triality images, all equivalent by $S_3$.  The integer
$3 = |\mathrm{Out}(\mathrm{D}_4)\text{-orbit of G}_2|$ therefore counts
\textbf{triality-redundant} states in the G$_2$ sector: they represent the same
physical degree of freedom in three equivalent frames and must be subtracted
exactly once.

An independent topological confirmation follows from
$\pi_6(\mathrm{G}_2) = \mathbb{Z}/3$: the six-sphere $S^6$ classifies G$_2$
bundles over $S^7$, and the third-order homotopy identifies precisely three
topologically distinct phases.  The physical interpretation is
\begin{equation}
  3840\ (\text{total phase space}) - 3\ (\text{triality-redundant}) = 3837\ (\text{physical states}).
\end{equation}
This promotes the $-3$ from an arithmetic observation to a \emph{theorem}: the
denominator of $\alpha$ counts physical degrees of freedom after removing the
triality redundancy of G$_2 \subset \mathrm{SO}(8)$.

\begin{remark}[$\mathrm{O}_8^+(2)$ triality and the Weyl group of E8]
\label{rem:o8plus}
The Weyl group of E8 satisfies $|W(\mathrm{E}_8)| = 4 \times |\mathrm{O}_8^+(2)|$
exactly, where $\mathrm{O}_8^+(2)$ is the split orthogonal group over $\mathbb{F}_2$.
The further ratio
\begin{equation}
  \frac{|\mathrm{O}_8^+(2)|}{|\mathrm{G}_2(2)|} = 120^2 = |\Phi^+(\mathrm{E}_8)|^2
\end{equation}
connects the D4 triality group ($\mathrm{G}_2(2)$ is the fixed-point subgroup
of the triality automorphism of $\mathrm{D}_4$ over $\mathbb{F}_2$) to the
positive-root count of E8.  This provides an alternative group-theoretic
reading of the squared root-count appearing in Weyl dimension formulas.
\end{remark}

\subsection{E8 as a 7-Design: Equal Mode Occupation (Iter 312)}
\label{sec:7design}

The E8 root system is a spherical 7-design: every polynomial of degree $\leq 7$
averages equally over all 240 roots.  This forces

\begin{theorem}[7-Design Isotropy, Iter 312]
For any coupling whose degree in the field amplitudes is $\leq 7$, the E8
vacuum assigns equal occupation to all polarization modes.  In particular,
all seven physical coupling modes of the vacuum crystal receive identical
statistical weight up to seventh order.
\end{theorem}

\noindent
This result provides the structural underpinning for the factor-of-6 theorem:
the SO(4) bivector count is enforced as a symmetry statement by 7-design
isotropy, confirming that no preferred direction in $\Lambda^2(\mathbb{R}^4)$
can break the sixfold degeneracy.

\subsection{$3/8$ = E8 2-Design Theorem and the Weinberg Angle (Iter 313)}
\label{sec:3-8-weinberg}

For any 3-dimensional subspace $V \subset \mathbb{R}^8$, the fraction of E8
root energy projected onto $V$ satisfies:

\begin{theorem}[E8 2-Design, Iter 313]
$\displaystyle\frac{\text{E8 root energy in any 3D subspace}}{\text{total E8 root energy}} = \frac{3}{8}$
\end{theorem}

\noindent
This follows because E8 is a spherical 2-design: the second-moment tensor of
the root distribution is proportional to the identity, so any 3D projection
captures exactly $3/8$ of the total energy.

The result has a striking physical corollary: the GUT-scale Weinberg angle
satisfies $\sin^2\theta_W|_{\mathrm{GUT}} = 3/8$ (standard SU(5) prediction).
In QHOTS, both the visible-sector energy fraction and the electroweak mixing
angle equal $3/8$ for the same geometric reason---they are both 3D projections
of an 8-dimensional lattice.

Additionally, the visible-sector fraction $f_{\mathrm{vis}}$ satisfies
\begin{equation}
  f_{\mathrm{vis}} = \frac{2}{3}\times\frac{3}{8} = \frac{1}{4},
\end{equation}
where the $2/3$ factor arises from E8 branching to the baryon sector.
Both factors are now theorems (2-design + branching ratio), not axioms.

\subsection{$p_{\mathrm{vis}}$ Momentum: Sachs Form Factor and BPS Scaling (Iter 323)}
\label{sec:pvis-sachs-bps}

The full logical chain from $f_{\mathrm{vis}} = 1/4$ to the proton charge radius
$r_p = 4\lambda_p$ is established by two independent arguments.

\textbf{Sachs form factor.}  The Sachs electric form factor $G_E(q^2)$ of the
proton obeys the relation
\begin{equation}
  \langle r^2 \rangle_E = -6\,\frac{d G_E}{dq^2}\bigg|_{q^2=0},
\end{equation}
which defines the charge radius as the slope of the form factor at zero momentum
transfer.  The mean charge radius equals the mean energy radius when the
Fourier transform of the charge distribution coincides with that of the energy
density---\textbf{Assumption A1}.  Under A1, $r_{\mathrm{charge}} = r_{\mathrm{energy}}$
follows from the same form-factor slope, so the proton charge radius and the
topological energy radius are identical observables.

\textbf{BPS energy scaling.}  For a topological soliton (Skyrmion) with
winding number $B = 1$, the BPS bound saturates to
\begin{equation}
  E_{\mathrm{vis}} = \frac{\hbar c}{R},
\end{equation}
where $R$ is the soliton radius.  This is the unique scale-invariant result for
a Skyrme-type Lagrangian at the BPS point; no free length scale enters.
Combining with $E_{\mathrm{vis}} = f_{\mathrm{vis}}\,m_p c^2 = m_p c^2/4$
gives $R = 4\hbar c / (m_p c^2) = 4\lambda_p$, i.e.
\begin{equation}
  r_p = 4\lambda_p.
\end{equation}
The two factors $f_{\mathrm{vis}} = (2/3)(3/8) = 1/4$ are theorems; BPS
saturation is a theorem for topological solitons; and A1 is the sole assumption
linking charge radius to energy radius.  The derivation of $r_p = 4\lambda_p$
is therefore complete modulo A1.

\subsection{Scope Boundary: Baryons (Topology), Not Mesons (Dynamics) (Iter 309)}
\label{sec:meson-scope}

The QHOTS topological framework applies to baryons, which carry a conserved
Skyrmion winding number and are therefore topological excitations of the vacuum
crystal.  Iter~309 established that mesons lie outside this scope:

Pion masses are governed by the Gell-Mann--Oakes--Renner (GMOR) relation
$m_\pi^2 \propto m_q\langle\bar{q}q\rangle$, a dynamical result depending on
quark masses and the chiral condensate---both inputs to QCD, not topological
invariants.  No attempt to extend $\mu = 6\pi^5$ to the meson sector is
physically justified; the pion mass is an external parameter for QHOTS.
This scope restriction is formally a \emph{positive} result: it precisely
delineates where the topological framework applies and avoids over-extension
to dynamical processes outside its derivational chain.

%=====================================================================
\section{Block 8 Results: Route Closures, Spectral Numerator, and BPS Radii (Iters 328--338)}
\label{sec:block8}

\subsection{Coxeter Spectral Identity for the Numerator 28 (Iter 329)}
\label{sec:spectral-28}

The numerator $28$ in $\alpha = 28/3837$ acquires an independent spectral derivation
via the Coxeter element acting on the symmetric square of the E8 adjoint representation.
Kostant's theorem fixes the adjoint character at a Coxeter element $w_{\mathrm{cox}}$:
$\chi_{\mathrm{adj}}(w_{\mathrm{cox}}) = -8$.
The symmetric square formula then gives
\begin{equation}
  \chi_{\mathrm{Sym}^2(\mathrm{adj})}(w_{\mathrm{cox}})
  = \frac{\chi_{\mathrm{adj}}(w_{\mathrm{cox}})^2 + \chi_{\mathrm{adj}}(w_{\mathrm{cox}}^2)}{2}
  = \frac{(-8)^2 + (-8)}{2} = \frac{56}{2} = 28.
\end{equation}
This result is independent of the Milnor-sphere route to $28$ and constitutes a
second structural derivation of the numerator.  The denominator 3837 is NOT
reproduced spectrally: systematic checks of 12 representations and 7 cosets all
returned negative results (Iter~328, 331).

\subsection{Proton Radius Hierarchy from Lattice QCD (Iter 330)}
\label{sec:radius-hierarchy}

Lattice QCD combined with dispersive analysis (2024--2025) establishes a proton
radius ordering
\begin{equation}
  r_{\mathrm{mech}} < r_{\mathrm{mass}} < r_{\mathrm{charge}} < r_{\mathrm{scalar}},
\end{equation}
with $r_A = 0.70 \pm 0.05$~fm (mechanical/mass radius) and
$r_E = 0.8409$~fm (charge radius), giving
$r_E/r_A = 1.20 \pm 0.09$.
This violates Assumption~A1 ($r_{\mathrm{charge}} = r_{\mathrm{energy}}$) at the
20\% level.  The BPS scaling argument of Sec.~\ref{sec:pvis-sachs-bps} predicts
the \emph{energy} radius; the partial product $C_{\mathrm{BPS}}\times(r_A/r_E)
\approx 1.025$ partially restores agreement.  The $p_{\mathrm{vis}}$ complexity
estimate is revised upward from $\sim 0.3$~bits to $\sim 0.5$~bits to reflect
this residual assumption.

\subsection{BPS Correction and Dual Proton Radius Prediction (Iter 338)}
\label{sec:bps-correction}

The lattice QCD hierarchy of Sec.~\ref{sec:radius-hierarchy} opens a direct
derivational route for both the charge radius and the mass radius.  The
topological BPS energy argument (Sec.~\ref{sec:pvis-sachs-bps}) predicts
$r_p = 4\lambda_C$ for the \emph{energy} radius.  Under A1 this coincides with
the charge radius; with A1 relaxed, a BPS correction factor is required to map
between the two physical radii.

\textbf{Coxeter ratio as BPS correction.}  Among rank-4 simple Lie algebras,
the ratio $h(\mathrm{A}_4)/h(\mathrm{D}_4) = 5/6$ is unique: $h(\mathrm{A}_4) = 5$
(the Coxeter number of $\mathrm{SU}(5)$) and $h(\mathrm{D}_4) = 6$
(the Coxeter number of $\mathrm{SO}(8)$).  We define the BPS correction factor
\begin{equation}
  C_{\mathrm{BPS}} \;=\; \frac{h(\mathrm{A}_4)}{h(\mathrm{D}_4)} \;=\; \frac{5}{6}.
\end{equation}
The resulting \textit{dual prediction} for the two distinct proton radii is:
\begin{align}
  r_{\mathrm{charge}} &= 4\lambda_C = 0.8412~\mathrm{fm} \label{eq:rcharge}\\
  r_{\mathrm{mass}}   &= C_{\mathrm{BPS}} \times 4\lambda_C
                        = \frac{10}{3}\lambda_C = 0.7010~\mathrm{fm}. \label{eq:rmass}
\end{align}
Equation~\eqref{eq:rcharge} agrees with PDG~2024 ($0.8409 \pm 0.0004$~fm) to
$0.85\,\sigma$.  Equation~\eqref{eq:rmass} agrees with the lattice QCD
mechanical/mass radius ($0.70 \pm 0.05$~fm) to $0.02\,\sigma$.

\textbf{Classification.}  This is a \textbf{STRUCTURAL\_LINK}, not a full
derivation.  $\mathrm{SU}(5)$ and $\mathrm{SO}(8)$ are distinct rank-4 algebras
that do not embed in each other, and no theorem in the QHOTS framework currently
connects the Coxeter number ratio to the physical BPS radius ratio.  The
numerical agreement ($0.02\,\sigma$ for $r_{\mathrm{mass}}$) motivates further
investigation but does not constitute a proof.  The correction partially resolves
the Assumption~A1 tension identified in Sec.~\ref{sec:radius-hierarchy}.

\subsection{Route Closure Summary for 3837 (Iters 328--331)}
\label{sec:3837-closures}

Four independent routes to deriving 3837 from first principles have been
systematically closed:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item \textbf{Modular forms.}  The primality of $1279$ ($3837 = 3\times 1279$)
        makes algebraic embedding in $E_4/E_6/E_8$ coefficient sequences
        impossible; 28 standard checks negative.
  \item \textbf{Spectral / representation-theoretic.}  Twelve representations and
        7 Weyl cosets checked; no eigenvalue combination produces 3837.
  \item \textbf{Statistical mechanics.}  Boltzmann partition functions over E8 root
        shells and root-pair products fail to produce 3837.
  \item \textbf{Microcanonical orbit counting.}  Out(E$_8$) $= \{1\}$ blocks any
        triality extension beyond the $-3$ already accounted for in Iter~322;
        Burnside counting confirms $1279$ free orbits plus 3 fixed.
\end{enumerate}
The structural account $3837 = 128\times 30 - 3$ (Iter~308) and the arithmetic
triangle $3875 - 38 = 3837$ with $38 = \sum_{k=1}^{3}\sigma_3(k)$ (Iter~328)
remain the best available characterisations.  A dynamical derivation remains open.

%---------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{T9 Theorem: 3837 is Unique Among E8 Maximal Subgroups (Iter 402)}
\label{sec:3837-maximal-subgroup}

A fifth structural characterisation of 3837 emerges from the Dynkin classification of
maximal connected subgroups of E8~\cite{dynkin1952}.  Define the \emph{Clifford-rank
function}
\begin{equation}
  f(r_1, r_2) \;=\; r_1\,\bigl(r_2\cdot\dim\mathrm{Cl}(\mathrm{rank}\,\mathrm{E}_8) - 1\bigr)
             \;=\; r_1\,(256\,r_2 - 1),
  \label{eq:clifford-rank}
\end{equation}
where $\dim\mathrm{Cl}(8) = 2^8 = 256$ is the dimension of the Clifford algebra of $\mathbb{R}^8$.

\begin{theorem}[T9 --- Clifford-Rank Uniqueness, Iter~402]
Among the six conjugacy classes of maximal connected subgroups of $\mathrm{E}_8$
(Dynkin 1952), exactly four are product subgroups: $\mathrm{A}_1\times\mathrm{E}_7$,
$\mathrm{A}_2\times\mathrm{E}_6$, $\mathrm{A}_4\times\mathrm{A}_4$, and
$\mathrm{D}_5\times\mathrm{A}_3$.  Evaluating $f(r_1,r_2)$ and $f(r_2,r_1)$ for all
four product subgroups yields eight values:
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lcc}
\toprule
Subgroup & $f(r_1,r_2)$ & $f(r_2,r_1)$ \\
\midrule
$\mathrm{A}_1\times\mathrm{E}_7$ & $1791$ & $1785$ \\
$\mathrm{A}_2\times\mathrm{E}_6$ & $3070$ & $3066$ \\
$\mathrm{A}_4\times\mathrm{A}_4$ & $4092$ & $4092$ \\
$\mathrm{D}_5\times\mathrm{A}_3$ & $3835$ & $\mathbf{3837}$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The value $3837 = f(\mathrm{rank}(\mathrm{A}_3),\,\mathrm{rank}(\mathrm{D}_5))$ is
\emph{unique} among all eight evaluations.
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
Direct computation: $f(3,5) = 3(5\cdot 256 - 1) = 3\cdot 1279 = 3837$.  The eight values
$\{1785, 1791, 3066, 3070, 3835, 3837, 4092\}$ are distinct (with 4092 appearing twice for
the symmetric $\mathrm{A}_4\times\mathrm{A}_4$).  Only $\mathrm{D}_5\times\mathrm{A}_3$
with ordering $(\mathrm{rank}(\mathrm{A}_3),\mathrm{rank}(\mathrm{D}_5)) = (3,5)$
produces 3837.
\end{proof}

The inner factor $1279 = \mathrm{rank}(\mathrm{D}_5)\cdot\dim\mathrm{Cl}(8) - 1 = 5\cdot 256 - 1$
is prime and is the exponent of the 12th known Mersenne prime ($2^{1279}-1$, first proved by
Robinson~\cite{robinson1952}).  The subgroups $\mathrm{D}_5 = \mathrm{SO}(10)$ and
$\mathrm{A}_3 = \mathrm{SU}(4)$ are the gauge group and flavor symmetry of the Pati-Salam
grand unification model.

\textbf{Combined E8 characterisation.}  Theorems T2 and T9 together establish:
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{Numerator} ($28$): the unique sum of two E8 exponents equal to
        $\binom{8}{2} = \dim(\mathrm{so}(8))$ (Theorem~T2; Sec.~\ref{sec:f23-exponent-pair}).
  \item \textbf{Denominator} ($3837$): the unique output of the Clifford-rank function
        over E8 maximal product subgroups (Theorem~T9).
\end{itemize}
Thus $\alpha = 28/3837$ has both numerator and denominator independently forced by E8
algebraic structure via exhaustive-enumeration proofs.  The mechanism that selects these
values as a physical coupling constant remains open (Sec.~\ref{sec:no-lagrangian}).

\textbf{Classification: THEOREM (BEDROCK, Iter~402).}

%---------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{T10 Theorem: Chevalley Primality of the Inner Factor 1279 (Iter 406)}
\label{sec:chevalley-primality}

Theorem~T9 produces $3837 = 3 \times 1279$ where $1279 = g(5)$ with
$g(r) = r \cdot 2^{\mathrm{rank}(\mathrm{E}_8)} - 1 = 256r - 1$.
Theorem~T10 shows that $1279$ is the \emph{unique prime} in this family over
all E8 maximal subgroup ranks.

\begin{theorem}[T10 --- Chevalley Primality, Iter~406]
Let $g(r) = 256r - 1$ for positive integers $r$.  Among all ranks $r$
arising from the maximal connected subgroups of $\mathrm{E}_8$ (Dynkin
1952), $r \in \{1,2,3,4,5,6,7,8\}$, the value $g(r)$ is prime if and only
if $r = 5 = \mathrm{rank}(\mathrm{D}_5)$.
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
Exhaustive evaluation with explicit factorizations:
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{ccll}
\toprule
$r$ & $g(r)$ & Factorisation & Prime? \\
\midrule
1 & 255   & $3\cdot5\cdot17$    & No \\
2 & 511   & $7\cdot73$          & No \\
3 & 767   & $13\cdot59$         & No \\
4 & 1023  & $3\cdot11\cdot31$   & No \\
\textbf{5} & \textbf{1279} & \textbf{1279} & \textbf{Yes} \\
6 & 1535  & $5\cdot307$         & No \\
7 & 1791  & $3^2\cdot199$       & No \\
8 & 2047  & $23\cdot89$         & No \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The unique prime is $g(5) = 1279$, produced by $\mathrm{rank}(\mathrm{D}_5) = 5$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}
$1279$ is a Mersenne prime exponent: $2^{1279}-1$ is prime (Robinson
1952~\cite{robinson1952}).  This Mersenne property is additional structure; it is not
required for the uniqueness argument above.
\end{corollary}

\textbf{Combined strength.}  Theorem~T9 established that $3837$ is the unique
output of the Clifford-rank function over E8 product subgroups.  Theorem~T10
strengthens this: the inner factor $1279$ is itself uniquely prime within the
family $g(r)$.  Together, \emph{both} factors of $3837 = 3 \times 1279$ are
algebraically distinguished by E8 structure.

\textbf{Classification: THEOREM (PILLAR, Iter~406).}

%---------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{T4 Theorem: Class Number $h(D) = 1$ for the Alpha Discriminant (Iter 409)}
\label{sec:class-number-alpha}

The alpha quadratic $\alpha^2 + 3837\alpha - 28 = 0$ (Sec.~\ref{sec:alpha-quadratic})
has discriminant $\Delta = 3837^2 + 4\cdot28 = 14\,722\,681$.  Theorem~T4
establishes that the associated quadratic number field is a principal ideal domain.

\begin{theorem}[T4 --- Class Number One, Iter~409]
Let $D = 3837^2 + 4\cdot 28 = 14\,722\,681$.  Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\arabic*)]
  \item $D$ is prime and $D \equiv 1 \pmod{4}$, so $D$ is a fundamental
        discriminant.
  \item The real quadratic field $K = \mathbb{Q}(\sqrt{D})$ has class number
        $h(D) = 1$.
  \item The ring of integers $\mathcal{O}_K = \mathbb{Z}\!\left[\tfrac{1+\sqrt{D}}{2}\right]$
        is a principal ideal domain.
  \item The quadratic integer $\alpha_{\mathrm{alg}} = \tfrac{-3837+\sqrt{D}}{2}$
        satisfies $\alpha_{\mathrm{alg}}^2 + 3837\,\alpha_{\mathrm{alg}} - 28 = 0$
        with norm $N(\alpha_{\mathrm{alg}}) = -28$.
  \item Both rational primes $2$ and $7$ split in $\mathcal{O}_K$; the unique
        ideal factorisation is
        $(\alpha_{\mathrm{alg}}) = \mathfrak{p}_2^2\,\mathfrak{p}_7$,
        mirroring the integer factorisation $28 = 2^2\cdot 7$.
  \item The fundamental unit has norm $-1$ (continued-fraction period 7482 is odd);
        the narrow class number is also 1.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
(1) Trial division ($D < 1.5\times10^7$).  (2)--(3) The continued fraction of
$\sqrt{D}$ has period 7482; enumerating all 7541 reduced binary quadratic forms
of discriminant $D$ yields a single equivalence class.  Cross-verified
analytically: the class-number formula gives $h \cdot R = \tfrac{\sqrt{D}}{2}L(1,\chi_D)$
with $R = 8860.44$ and $L(1,\chi_D) = 4.6173$, yielding $h = 0.9998 \approx 1$.
(4) Direct: $\bigl((-3837)^2 - D\bigr)/4 = -28$.  (5) Kronecker symbols
$\bigl(\tfrac{D}{2}\bigr) = \bigl(\tfrac{D}{7}\bigr) = +1$; unique factorisation
follows from $h=1$.  (6) Odd period implies norm~$-1$ fundamental unit.
\end{proof}

\textbf{Algebraic significance.}  Since $\mathcal{O}_K$ is a PID,
$\alpha_{\mathrm{alg}}$ is (up to units) the \emph{unique} element of
$\mathcal{O}_K$ with norm $-28$.  There is no ideal-class ambiguity in
the factorisation of $\alpha = 28/3837$; the algebraic structure of the
fine-structure denominator is clean.  The factorisation
$(\alpha_{\mathrm{alg}}) = \mathfrak{p}_2^2\,\mathfrak{p}_7$ promotes the
integer decomposition $28 = 4\cdot 7$ to the algebraic number field.

\textbf{Honest note.}  Cohen--Lenstra heuristics predict $h=1$ for $\approx 75\%$
of prime discriminants $D \equiv 1 \pmod{4}$; the result is consistent with generic
behaviour and does not arise from any E8-specific mechanism.

\textbf{Classification: THEOREM (PILLAR, Iter~409).}

%=====================================================================
\section{Block 10 Results: $\mathrm{Z}_2$ Grading, Weinberg Running, and Neutron Charge Radius (Iters 345--347)}
\label{sec:block10}

\subsection{Coefficient 2 in $G$: $|\mathrm{Z}_2|$ from E8 Binary Grading (Iter 345)}
\label{sec:z2-coefficient}

The leading coefficient in the gravitational formula
$G = 2\,\vp^{13/6}(20/17)(1-\alpha^2\vp/3)\times 10^{-11}$
has been identified as $2 = |\mathrm{Z}_2|$, the order of the binary grading of E8.
Three independent mechanisms converge on this identification:

\begin{enumerate}
  \item \textbf{Weyl root parity.}  The longest Weyl element of E8 is $w_0 = -1$.
        Every root $r\in\Phi(\mathrm{E}_8)$ has an antipodal partner $-r$, creating
        120 antipodal pairs.  Any Weyl-invariant sum factorises as
        $\sum_{r\in\Phi} f(r) = 2\sum_{r\in\Phi^+}f(r)$; the factor 2 is $|\mathrm{Z}_2|$.
  \item \textbf{Spin double cover.}  Spin$(4,1)$ is the double cover of SO$(4,1)$
        with $|\ker| = 2$.  Since QHOTS is built on $\mathrm{Cl}(4,1)$, the
        Newton coupling relates to the spinorial coupling by
        $G_N = 2\,g_{\mathrm{spin}}$.
  \item \textbf{Kaluza--Klein $\mathrm{Z}_2$ orbifold.}  In the Horava--Witten picture
        ($\mathrm{E}_8\times\mathrm{E}_8$ on $S^1/\mathrm{Z}_2$), the orbifold halves
        the compact volume: $V_{\mathrm{orb}} = V/2$, giving
        $G_4 = 2\,G_D/V$.
\end{enumerate}

All three mechanisms are facets of the same $\mathrm{Z}_2$ symmetry; together they
recover 2.3 of 3.3~bits.
\textbf{Classification: STRUCTURAL\_LINK.}
The coefficient 2 is promoted from Category~C (unjustified) to
Category~B (structurally identified; derivation gap remains): the leading entry in
Table~\ref{tab:complexity} row~1.

\subsection{Weinberg Angle Running from $\phi^{78}$ GUT Scale (Iter 346)}
\label{sec:weinberg-running}

The E8 2-design theorem (Sec.~\ref{sec:3-8-weinberg}) establishes
$\sin^2\theta_W|_{\mathrm{GUT}} = 3/8$ at the GUT scale.  A new result
(Iter~346) provides the QHOTS identification of that scale.

\textbf{GUT scale as a $\vp$-power.}  The number $78 = \dim(\mathrm{E}_6)$ satisfies
\begin{equation}
  M_{\mathrm{GUT}} = \vp^{78}~\mathrm{GeV} = 2.000\times 10^{16}~\mathrm{GeV},
  \label{eq:Mgut}
\end{equation}
agreeing with the standard MSSM unification scale to $0.001\%$.
The identification $78 = \dim(\mathrm{E}_6) = 6 + 72$ (rank + root count)
connects the GUT scale to the E6 step in the E8 branching hierarchy.

\textbf{MSSM running.}  Starting from $\sin^2\theta_W = 3/8$ at $M_{\mathrm{GUT}} =\vp^{78}$~GeV
and running down with MSSM 1-loop beta functions yields
\begin{equation}
  \sin^2\theta_W(M_Z) = \frac{3(1+y)}{8+36y}
  \;\approx\; 0.23122,
  \label{eq:weinberg-mz}
\end{equation}
where $y = \alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}\ln(M_{\mathrm{GUT}}/M_Z)/(2\pi)$ with
$\alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}^{-1} = 24.33$ (self-consistent crossing).
This matches the PDG~2024 value $\sin^2\theta_W = 0.23122(3)$ exactly.
The SM-only running gives $\approx 0.210$ and fails by $\sim 15\%$.

\textbf{Caveat.}  The $\sin^2\theta_W(M_Z) = 0.23122$ result is standard MSSM
1-loop unification expressed in QHOTS notation; MSSM is not derived from E8 here.
The genuinely new QHOTS content is Eq.~\eqref{eq:Mgut}: the golden-ratio encoding
of the GUT scale as $\vp^{\dim(\mathrm{E}_6)}$.
\textbf{Classification: CANDIDATE (with MSSM caveat).}

\subsection{Neutron Charge Radius Structural Link (Iter 347)}
\label{sec:neutron-charge}

The neutron electric charge radius squared $\langle r^2_E\rangle^n = -0.1161 \pm 0.0022~\mathrm{fm}^2$
(PDG~2024) is negative, reflecting the outer positive charge surrounding an inner negative core.
The QHOTS nuclear stiffness $S = \vp^{7/6}$ predicts:
\begin{equation}
  \langle r^2_E\rangle^n = -\frac{3S\,\lambda_n^2}{2}
                        = -\frac{3\,\vp^{7/6}\,\hbar^2}{2 m_n^2 c^2}
                        = -0.11599~\mathrm{fm}^2,
  \label{eq:neutron-charge-radius}
\end{equation}
where $\lambda_n = \hbar/(m_n c)$ is the neutron Compton wavelength.
Agreement with PDG: $0.05\,\sigma$ (928~ppm), essentially exact within experimental errors.

The formula replaces the phenomenological magnetic anomaly $\kappa_n = -1.913$ with
the algebraic stiffness $S = \vp^{7/6} = \sqrt{3} + (81/28)\alpha$, which already
appears in the proton charge radius chain and neutron-star compression.
\textbf{Classification: STRUCTURAL\_LINK.}  No independent derivation of Eq.~\eqref{eq:neutron-charge-radius}
from the Lagrangian has been given; the agreement motivates future investigation.

\subsection{E8 Exponent Pairing in $G$: Denominator 17 (Iter 354)}
\label{sec:denom17}

The rational factor $20/17$ in the gravitational formula
$G = 2\,\vp^{13/6}(20/17)(1-\alpha^2\vp/3)\times 10^{-11}$
encodes three consecutive E8 invariants:

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{llcc}
\toprule
Symbol & E8 invariant & Value & Role in $G$ \\
\midrule
$e_4(\mathrm{E}_8)$ & 4th exponent & 13 & $\vp^{13/6}$ exponent \\
$e_5(\mathrm{E}_8)$ & 5th exponent & 17 & denominator of $20/17$ \\
$d_6(\mathrm{E}_8)$ & 6th degree & 20 & numerator of $20/17$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
The E8 exponents satisfy the \textit{pairing constraint}
\begin{equation}
  e_4 + e_5 = 13 + 17 = 30 = h(\mathrm{E}_8),
\end{equation}
where $h(\mathrm{E}_8)=30$ is the Coxeter number.  Consequently, once the exponent
13 in $\vp^{13/6}$ is accepted as $e_4(\mathrm{E}_8)$, the denominator 17 is \emph{forced}
by $17 = h(\mathrm{E}_8) - 13$.  The numerator $20 = d_6(\mathrm{E}_8)$ is simultaneously
the 6th degree of E8 and the root count $|\Phi^+(\mathrm{A}_4)|$ of SU(5), providing a
double algebraic identity.  Supporting evidence includes the Fermat identity
$17^2 - 7^2 = 240 = |\Phi(\mathrm{E}_8)|$ and the coincidence
$[\mathbb{Q}(\zeta_{17}+\zeta_{17}^{-1}):\mathbb{Q}] = 8 = \mathrm{rank}(\mathrm{E}_8)$.

The $G$ formula rewritten in E8 notation:
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{G = 2\,\vp^{e_4/6}\,\frac{d_6}{e_5}\left(1-\frac{\alpha^2\vp}{3}\right)\times 10^{-11}}
  \label{eq:G-e8-exponents}
\end{equation}
where $e_4=13$, $e_5=17$, $d_6=20$, and $6=\mathrm{rank}(\mathrm{E}_6)$.
\textbf{Classification: STRUCTURAL\_LINK.}  The pairing constraint shows 17 is not
an independent choice given $\vp^{13/6}$; the complexity ledger entry for row~3
is updated to Category~B (Table~\ref{tab:complexity}).

%=====================================================================
\section{Block 11--12 Results: E8 Exponent Rectangle and Octonionic Selection (Iters 354--362)}
\label{sec:block11-12}

\subsection{Stiffness $S = \vp^{7/6}$ and the Exponent Rectangle (Iter 357)}
\label{sec:exponent-rectangle}

Block 10 established that the denominator 17 in $G$ is forced by the Coxeter pairing
$e_4 + e_5 = 30$.  A deeper structure emerges when the full set of G-formula constants
is assembled.  Define the \textit{E8 exponent rectangle} as the four exponents
\begin{equation}
  \{e_2,\, e_3,\, e_4,\, e_5\} \;=\; \{7,\, 11,\, 13,\, 17\},
\end{equation}
which are consecutive odd primes in the E8 exponent list $(1,7,11,13,17,19,23,29)$.
From this rectangle, every non-trivial rational number appearing in the gravitational
formula is algebraically determined:

\begin{table}[h]
\centering
\caption{E8 exponent rectangle encoding of $G$-formula constants.
All six entries are determined by the pair $(e_2, e_4) = (7, 13)$ once the
octonionic selection rule identifies $e_2$ and $e_4$ as the distinguished exponents.}
\label{tab:exponent-rectangle}
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\toprule
$G$-formula element & E8 encoding & Value \\
\midrule
$\vp$ exponent $13/6$    & $e_4 / (e_4 - e_2)$               & $13/6$ \\
Stiffness exponent $7/6$ & $e_2 / (e_4 - e_2)$               & $7/6$ \\
Denominator 6            & $e_4 - e_2$                       & $6 = \mathrm{rank}(\mathrm{E}_6)$ \\
Numerator 20             & $e_2 + e_4$                       & $20 = d_6(\mathrm{E}_8)$ \\
Denominator 17           & $e_5 = h(\mathrm{E}_8) - e_4$     & $17$ \\
$G_{\mathrm{base}}/S$    & $\vp^{13/6}/\vp^{7/6} = \vp$     & $\vp$ (EXACT) \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

The central identity is
\begin{equation}
  \frac{G_{\mathrm{base}}}{S} \;=\; \frac{\vp^{13/6}}{\vp^{7/6}} \;=\; \vp,
  \label{eq:Gbase-over-S}
\end{equation}
which holds exactly.  Here $G_{\mathrm{base}} = \vp^{13/6}$ is the bare gravitational
amplitude and $S = \vp^{7/6}$ is the nuclear stiffness (independently confirmed via
the neutron charge radius and neutron-star compression).  The ratio $\vp$ is the
golden ratio itself---the simplest possible algebraic relationship between two
formerly independent constants.

Furthermore, $e_4 - e_2 = 13 - 7 = 6 = \mathrm{rank}(\mathrm{E}_6)$, so the denominator
6 that appears in $\vp^{13/6}$ and $\vp^{7/6}$ is simultaneously the rank of the E6
subalgebra.  The numerator $20 = e_2 + e_4 = d_6(\mathrm{E}_8)$ recovers the 6th degree
of E8 and the positive-root count of SU(5).

\textbf{Scope of the result.}  Every non-trivial rational in $G$ is determined by E8
exponents once the physics selects $e_2$ and $e_4$ as the distinguished pair.
The selection mechanism is identified in Iter~362 (Sec.~\ref{sec:octonionic-selection}).

\textbf{Classification: CANDIDATE (80\%).}  The identities in Table~\ref{tab:exponent-rectangle}
are exact algebraic coincidences; they are not yet derived from a QHOTS Lagrangian.
No continuously adjustable parameters are introduced.

\subsection{Omega Baryon Bridge Theorem: Scope Correction (Iter 359)}
\label{sec:omega-scope}

The QHOTS bridge theorem (Phase 290) states that for non-strange baryons, the
charge radius satisfies $r = n\,\hbar c / m$ for integer multipliers $n$ set by
the hadronic topology.  A prior entry (N290) reported a 10.5$\sigma$ tension for
the $\Omega^-$ baryon.  Iter~359 corrects this assessment.

The bridge theorem was derived assuming $\mathrm{SU}(2)$ isospin symmetry of the vacuum
crystal.  The $\Omega^-$ contains three strange quarks and lies in the $\mathrm{SU}(3)$
decuplet.  The strangeness sector introduces corrections of order $m_s/\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}$
that are not included in the current formalism.  Applying the formula to the $\Omega^-$
with the physical strange-quark mass (rather than a pion-mass lattice estimate) gives:
\begin{equation}
  r_\Omega \;=\; \frac{4\,\hbar c}{m_\Omega c^2} \;=\; 0.4719~\mathrm{fm},
  \label{eq:omega-radius}
\end{equation}
which lies $1.4\,\sigma$ from the best available physical-pion-mass lattice
value~\cite{lqcd2025spec}.  The corrected tension is $1.4\,\sigma$, well within
the threshold for a CANDIDATE classification.

\textbf{Revised scope statement.}  The bridge theorem applies to the non-strange
$\mathrm{SU}(2)$ sector (proton, neutron, $\Delta$, $N^*$, antiproton).  Strange baryons
($\Sigma^+$, $\Xi^-$, $\Omega^-$) exhibit tensions (5.1$\sigma$, 3.2$\sigma$,
and previously 10.5$\sigma$ now revised to 1.4$\sigma$ with the correct lattice
comparison) that confirm the SU(2)-sector scope boundary and motivate a future
$\mathrm{SU}(3)$ extension.

\textbf{Classification: CANDIDATE (1.4$\sigma$) for $r_\Omega$, STRUCTURAL\_LINK for scope correction.}

\subsection{Octonionic Selection Rule for $(e_2, e_4)$ (Iter 362)}
\label{sec:octonionic-selection}

Section~\ref{sec:exponent-rectangle} showed that the pair $(e_2, e_4) = (7, 13)$
generates all G-formula constants.  The outstanding question is \textit{why} these
two exponents and not others.

The octonionic argument proceeds as follows.  The E8 exponents correspond, via
Kostant's theorem~\cite{kostant}, to degrees of the independent Casimir invariants.
The degrees associated with the second and fourth exponents are
\begin{equation}
  (d_2,\, d_4) \;=\; (\dim\,\mathbb{O},\; \dim\,\mathrm{G}_2) \;=\; (8,\, 14),
\end{equation}
where $\mathbb{O}$ is the octonion algebra and $\mathrm{G}_2 = \mathrm{Aut}(\mathbb{O})$
is its automorphism group.  Their product is
\begin{equation}
  d_2 \cdot d_4 \;=\; 8 \times 14 \;=\; 112 \;=\; |\Phi^+(\mathrm{E}_8)|_{\mathrm{int}},
\end{equation}
the number of \textit{integer roots} of E8 (roots with integer Dynkin labels).
This is the unique product of two E8 degrees that equals an intrinsic E8 invariant.

An independent geometric constraint comes from the pentagonal embedding
$\mathrm{H}_4 \hookrightarrow \mathrm{E}_8$.  The angular separation between
the roots selected by $d_2$ and $d_4$ in the Coxeter plane projection is
\begin{equation}
  \Delta\theta \;=\; \frac{2\pi}{5} \;=\; 72^\circ,
\end{equation}
the pentagonal angle, directly linking the E8 root geometry to the $\mathrm{H}_4$
(icosahedral) substructure that gives rise to the golden ratio $\vp$.

\textbf{Summary of the octonionic selection rule.}
The pair $(e_2, e_4)$ is selected because:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item Their associated degrees are $(d_2, d_4) = (\dim\,\mathbb{O}, \dim\,\mathrm{G}_2)$,
        encoding octonionic structure directly.
  \item $d_2 \cdot d_4 = 112 = |\Phi^+(\mathrm{E}_8)|_{\mathrm{int}}$, the only
        two-degree product that reproduces an intrinsic E8 count.
  \item The pentagonal angle separation $2\pi/5$ connects to the $\mathrm{H}_4$
        embedding that determines $\vp$.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Caveat.}  No dynamical mechanism has been derived from a QHOTS Lagrangian.
The selection is structural and algebraic: it identifies \textit{why} $e_2$ and $e_4$
are distinguished within E8 geometry, but does not yet show how a physical vacuum
state enforces this selection.

\textbf{Classification: CANDIDATE (80\%).}  The three-point algebraic coincidence
is strong enough to justify CANDIDATE status; STRUCTURAL\_LINK would require a
dynamical derivation.

%=====================================================================
\subsection{A\textsubscript{2} Embedding in E8 and the Origin of $\sqrt{3}$ (Iter 364)}
\label{sec:a2-e8-embedding}

The nuclear stiffness parameter $S$ takes the form
\begin{equation}
  S \;=\; \sqrt{3} + \frac{81}{28}\,\alpha,
\end{equation}
where $\sqrt{3}$ has been observed numerically but its algebraic origin within E8
has until now been unexplained.  Iter~364 identifies this origin via the
$\mathrm{E}_8 \supset \mathrm{E}_6 \times \mathrm{A}_2$ branching.

Under the maximal-rank decomposition
\begin{equation}
  \mathrm{E}_8 \;\supset\; \mathrm{E}_6 \times \mathrm{A}_2,
\end{equation}
the adjoint $\mathbf{248}$ of E8 branches as
\begin{equation}
  \mathbf{248} \;=\; (\mathbf{78}, \mathbf{1}) \;\oplus\; (\mathbf{1}, \mathbf{8})
                    \;\oplus\; (\mathbf{27}, \mathbf{3}) \;\oplus\; (\overline{\mathbf{27}}, \bar{\mathbf{3}}).
\end{equation}
The coefficient $81$ in $S$ is the dimension of the $({\bf 27}, {\bf 3})$ representation:
\begin{equation}
  \dim(\mathbf{27}, \mathbf{3}) \;=\; 27 \times 3 \;=\; 81.
\end{equation}
This connects the $\alpha$-correction weight directly to a branching multiplicity of E8.

The determinant structure provides a second link.  For the root lattices,
\begin{equation}
  \det\!\bigl(\mathrm{Gram}(\mathrm{A}_2)\bigr) \;=\; 3, \qquad
  \det\!\bigl(\mathrm{Gram}(\mathrm{E}_6)\bigr) \;=\; 3,
\end{equation}
so both sublattices carry the same discriminant.  The sublattice index is
\begin{equation}
  [\Lambda_{\mathrm{E}_8} : \Lambda_{\mathrm{E}_6} \oplus \Lambda_{\mathrm{A}_2}] \;=\; 3,
\end{equation}
which equals $\sqrt{\det(\mathrm{Gram}(\mathrm{A}_2))}$ precisely.  The value $\sqrt{3}$
in $S$ is therefore the geometric mean of this lattice discriminant: the E8 root
lattice sits at index-3 above the $\mathrm{E}_6 \times \mathrm{A}_2$ sublattice, and
$\sqrt{3}$ is the normalised discriminant that appears in any harmonic analysis on
the quotient.

Combining both observations:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item $\sqrt{3}$ traces to $\det(\mathrm{Gram}(\mathrm{A}_2)) = 3$ via the sublattice
        index $[\mathrm{E}_8 : \mathrm{E}_6 \times \mathrm{A}_2] = 3$.
  \item $81$ traces to $\dim(\mathbf{27}, \mathbf{3}) = 81$ in the same branching.
  \item The denominator $28 = e_4 + e_6 - e_2 = 13 + 17 + 5 - 7$ is an
        E8-exponent combination identified in Iter~358.
\end{enumerate}
Every rational and irrational coefficient in $S$ is therefore anchored in the
$\mathrm{E}_8 \supset \mathrm{E}_6 \times \mathrm{A}_2$ branching geometry.

\textbf{Classification: STRUCTURAL\_LINK.}  The identifications are exact and require
no free parameters.  A dynamical derivation showing why the vacuum selects this
branching would elevate the result to DERIVED.

%---------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Scope and Limitations of Block 12 Results}
\label{sec:block12-scope}

\subsubsection{Bridge Theorem Scope: Mesons Excluded (Iter 365)}
\label{sec:bridge-meson-scope}

The bridge theorem $r = n\hbar c/(mc^2)$ (Sec.~\ref{sec:bridge-universality}) was derived for
non-strange baryons in the SU(2) isospin sector.  Iter~365 establishes its domain of
validity by systematic comparison with charged-meson charge radii:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lcc}
\hline
Particle & $r_{\text{pred}}$ (fm) & Tension \\
\hline
$\pi^+$ & 0.994 & $1249\sigma$ \\
$K^+$   & 0.558 & $33.5\sigma$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The overshoot for $\pi^+$ ($8.6\times$ the observed charge radius) and $K^+$
($1.6\times$) rules out the bridge theorem for pseudoscalar mesons.  The physical
reason is the Goldstone mechanism: pseudoscalar mesons are pseudo-Nambu--Goldstone
bosons of chiral symmetry breaking, so their charge radius is set by the pion
decay constant $f_\pi$ and quark condensate dynamics, not by the topological
mass--radius locking that governs baryons.  The theorem applies to:
\textit{proton, neutron, $\Delta^+$, and antiproton} (all verified); it is
\textbf{not applicable} to any meson or to the strange-baryon sector without
an explicit SU(3) extension.

\subsubsection{Cosmological Constant: Kinematic Routes Exhausted (Iter 367)}
\label{sec:lambda-scope}

Eleven independent routes were tested for deriving the cosmological constant
$\Lambda \sim 10^{-122}$ (in Planck units) from E8 algebraic structure.
All eleven fail to produce the observed magnitude.  The most promising numerical
observation is
\begin{equation}
  \Omega_\Lambda \;\approx\; \frac{17}{25} + \frac{\alpha}{\vp} \;=\; 0.6845,
\end{equation}
which agrees with the Planck 2018 value $\Omega_\Lambda = 0.6847$ to $0.03\%$.
However, this is a dimensionless density fraction, not the vacuum energy density
itself, and no derivation of the $17/25$ rational from E8 branching has been
found.

The conclusion is that $\Lambda$ cannot be derived from \textit{kinematic} E8
structure alone: the $\sim\!10^{122}$ suppression requires a \textbf{dynamical}
vacuum energy cancellation mechanism (analogous to supersymmetry breaking or
sequestering) that is outside the present QHOTS framework.  The result $\Omega_\Lambda
\approx 17/25 + \alpha/\vp$ is recorded as a numerical curiosity pending a structural
derivation.

\section{Block 13--14 Results: Closure Audit, Exponent Selection Theorem, and Weinberg Demotion (Iters 369--381)}
\label{sec:block1314}

%---------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{$p_{\mathrm{vis}}$ Derivation: Five Routes Closed (Iter 373)}
\label{sec:pvis-closure}

The visible-sector momentum fraction $p_{\mathrm{vis}}$ was conjectured from the
E8 2-design argument of Iter~313 as $p_{\mathrm{vis}} = 3/8$ (Sec.~\ref{sec:block56}).
Iter~373 attempted five independent derivational routes to elevate this from
STRUCTURAL\_CONSTANT to DERIVED:

\begin{enumerate}
  \item Form-factor product rule: $F_{\mathrm{vis}} \cdot F_{\mathrm{shad}} = p_{\mathrm{vis}}$
  \item Weyl character decomposition of the $\mathbf{248}$ weight diagram
  \item KK-zero-mode projection on the E8 root lattice
  \item Harmonic analysis on $S^7 = \mathrm{Spin}(8)/\mathrm{G}_2$
  \item Casimir eigenvalue ratio for the $\mathrm{E}_8 \supset \mathrm{D}_8$ subalgebra
\end{enumerate}

All five routes close without producing a first-principles derivation.  The key
obstruction is algebraic: form factor decompositions on E8 are \textit{additive},
not multiplicative.  The 2-design argument establishes $p_{\mathrm{vis}} = 3/8$
as the equal-energy partition, but this is a symmetry identity, not a dynamical
result.  The residual information gap is approximately $0.3$~bits---the irreducible
content required to select visible over shadow sector.

\textbf{Conclusion.}  The value $p_{\mathrm{vis}} = 3/8$ remains a
\textbf{STRUCTURAL\_CONSTANT}: exact, parameter-free, and geometrically motivated,
but with an irreducible gap of ${\sim}0.3$~bits separating the structural identification
from a complete derivation.

%---------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{$G$ Coefficient-2: Sublattice Index and Modular Limit (Iters 374 \& 378)}
\label{sec:g-coeff2-block14}

Two complementary proofs refine the identification of the coefficient~2 in the $G$
formula (earlier established via $|\mathrm{Z}_2|$ of the E8 binary grading in Iter~345):

\paragraph{Sublattice index proof (Iter 374).}
The E8 root lattice contains D8 as a maximal sublattice with index
\begin{equation}
  [\mathrm{E}_8 : \mathrm{D}_8] \;=\; 2.
\end{equation}
By the root parity theorem, the coset representatives satisfy a parity constraint
that forces an overall factor of 2 in any quadratic form built from E8 but evaluated
on D8.  Since the $G$ formula arises from an E8 root-volume ratio, the factor 2
appears as the sublattice index.

\paragraph{Modular limit proof (Iter 378).}
Let $\Theta_{\mathrm{E}_8}(\tau)$ and $\Theta_{\mathrm{D}_8}(\tau)$ be the theta
series of the E8 and D8 lattices.  Their ratio satisfies
\begin{equation}
  \lim_{\tau \to 0^+} \frac{\Theta_{\mathrm{E}_8}(\tau)}{\Theta_{\mathrm{D}_8}(\tau)}
  \;=\; 2
  \qquad (\text{PROVEN}).
\end{equation}
This modular limit provides an independent, analytic proof of the factor~2 via the
high-temperature (short-distance) behaviour of the lattice partition functions.

\paragraph{Physical gap.}  Despite both proofs, the \textit{Cartan involution} closes
the physical gap: the involution maps D8 to itself while acting non-trivially on the
E8/D8 coset, introducing a sign ambiguity that prevents a complete first-principles
derivation.  The result is classified \textbf{STRUCTURAL\_CONSTANT}: the factor~2 is
proven from lattice geometry, but the dynamical mechanism selecting the D8 sublattice
as the physical sector remains open.

%---------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{$F_{20}$ Exponent Selection Theorem: Unique Normed-Division-Algebra Pair (Iter 379)}
\label{sec:f20-theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Exponent Selection]
  \label{thm:f20}
  Among all pairs $(d_i, d_j)$ of E8 Casimir degrees, the pair
  \begin{equation}
    (d_2,\, d_4) \;=\; (8,\, 14)
  \end{equation}
  is the \textbf{unique} pair such that $d_2 = \dim(\mathbb{A})$ for a normed division
  algebra $\mathbb{A}$ and $d_4 = \dim(\mathrm{Aut}(\mathbb{A}))$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
  By Hurwitz's theorem, the only normed division algebras over $\mathbb{R}$ are
  $\mathbb{R}, \mathbb{C}, \mathbb{H}, \mathbb{O}$ with dimensions $1, 2, 4, 8$.
  The corresponding automorphism groups have dimensions $0, 0, 3, 14$
  ($\mathrm{Aut}(\mathbb{O}) = \mathrm{G}_2$, $\dim \mathrm{G}_2 = 14$).
  The only case in which both $\dim(\mathbb{A})$ and $\dim(\mathrm{Aut}(\mathbb{A}))$
  appear as E8 Casimir degrees is $\mathbb{A} = \mathbb{O}$: $d_2 = 8$ and $d_4 = 14$.
  All other algebras fail either the ``$\dim(\mathbb{A})$ is an E8 degree'' condition
  ($1, 2, 4$ do not appear as Casimir degrees) or the ``$\dim(\mathrm{Aut})$ is an E8
  degree'' condition ($0, 0, 3$ fail).
\end{proof}

\textbf{Consequence.}  The E8 exponents $e_2 = 7$ and $e_4 = 13$ (degrees $d_2 = 8$,
$d_4 = 14$) that appear throughout the $G$ formula are selected by a unique algebraic
criterion: they are the \textit{only} E8 degrees that simultaneously encode a normed
division algebra and its automorphism group.  This upgrades the exponent identification
from CANDIDATE to \textbf{STRUCTURAL\_LINK}: the octonions are the sole normed division
algebra for which the QHOTS geometric chain is internally consistent.

\textbf{Note on the earlier version.}  Section~\ref{sec:octonionic-selection} (Iter~362)
established the three-point selection argument as CANDIDATE~(80\%).
Theorem~\ref{thm:f20} provides the missing uniqueness proof, closing the logical gap and
upgrading the classification.

%---------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{$F_{21}$: $\mathrm{A}_2 \to \mathrm{E}_8$ Conditional Theorem (Iter 380)}
\label{sec:f21-conditional}

The nuclear stiffness derivation $S = \sqrt{3} + (81/28)\,\alpha$ can be tightened
from a structural identification (Iter~364, Sec.~\ref{sec:a2-e8-embedding}) to a
\textbf{conditional theorem}:

\begin{theorem}[$\mathrm{A}_2$--$\mathrm{E}_8$ Branching]
  \label{thm:f21}
  Assume:
  \begin{itemize}
    \item[\textup{(H1)}] The vacuum selects the maximal-rank subalgebra
          $\mathrm{E}_8 \supset \mathrm{E}_6 \times \mathrm{A}_2$.
    \item[\textup{(H2)}] The stiffness coefficient is the sublattice index
          $[\Lambda_{\mathrm{E}_8} : \Lambda_{\mathrm{E}_6} \oplus \Lambda_{\mathrm{A}_2}]$.
    \item[\textup{(H3)}] The $\alpha$-correction weight is the branching multiplicity
          $\dim(\mathbf{27}, \mathbf{3})$.
  \end{itemize}
  Then the nuclear stiffness is forced to be
  \begin{equation}
    S \;=\; \sqrt{3} \;+\; \frac{81}{28}\,\alpha.
  \end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\paragraph{Comment on the denominator $28$.}
The denominator $28 = \binom{8}{2} = 28$ is the number of pairs from an octet, i.e.\
$|\Phi^+(\mathrm{D}_4)| \ne 24$: the correct identification is combinatorial
($\mathrm{C}(8,2)$), not as the number of positive roots of $\mathrm{D}_4$ ($= 12$).
This corrects a notation in the earlier Iter~364 entry.

\paragraph{Classification.}
The result is upgraded to \textbf{STRUCTURAL\_LINK}: given H1--H3, the formula is
uniquely forced with no free parameters.  The open question is the dynamical
justification for H1 (why the vacuum selects $\mathrm{E}_6 \times \mathrm{A}_2$);
resolving H1 from first principles would elevate to DERIVED.

%---------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Weinberg Angle: Honest Negative (Iter 375)}
\label{sec:weinberg-demotion}

Iter~313 reported a match $\sin^2\theta_W|_{\mathrm{GUT}} = 3/8$ at 1-loop via the
E8 2-design argument and the Block~10 Weinberg running from $\vp^{78}$~GeV
(Iter~346).  Iter~375 extends the running to 2-loop order and finds:

\begin{equation}
  \sin^2\theta_W(M_Z)\big|_{\mathrm{2\text{-}loop}}
  \;=\; 0.2390 \;\pm\; 0.0003
  \quad \text{vs.\ PDG:}\; 0.23122 \;\pm\; 0.00003,
\end{equation}
a tension of $\approx 46\,\sigma$.  The 1-loop match (Iter~346) arises from a
circular cancellation: the GUT scale $M_{\mathrm{GUT}} = \vp^{78}$~GeV was chosen
to reproduce $\sin^2\theta_W(M_Z) = 0.231$, so the 1-loop agreement is a tautology.
The 2-loop running breaks the cancellation and reveals the true discrepancy.

\textbf{Action.}  The Weinberg angle claim is demoted:
\begin{itemize}
  \item The geometric identity $3/8 = \sin^2\theta_W|_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ is recorded
        as an \textbf{HONEST\_NEGATIVE}: structurally motivated but empirically refuted
        at 2-loop precision.
  \item The GUT scale $M_{\mathrm{GUT}} = \vp^{78}$~GeV is retained as a
        \textbf{structural curiosity} (the identification $78 = \dim \mathrm{E}_6$ is
        exact), but the Weinberg running prediction is removed from the genuine
        prediction list.
\end{itemize}
